href="#cite_note-wb-gini-3">[3]</a></sup><br/><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:orange">medium</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+1</span> (<a href="/wiki/West_Africa_Time" title="West Africa Time">WAT</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_Angola" title="Telephone numbers in Angola">+244</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:AO" title="ISO 3166-2:AO">AO</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.ao" title=".ao">.ao</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Angola</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="/&#609;/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">&#609;</span><span title="/o&#650;/: \'o\' in \'code\'">o&#650;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Angola-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/En-Angola-pronunciation.ogg" title="En-Angola-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <small>Portuguese:&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[&#592;&#771;&#712;&#609;&#596;l&#592;]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Angola</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Rep&#250;blica de Angola</i>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kikongo" title="Kikongo">Kikongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umbundu_language" title="Umbundu language">Umbundu</a>: <i lang="umb">Repubilika ya Ngola</i>), is a west-coast country of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">south</a>-<a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">central Africa</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_area" title="List of African countries by area">seventh-largest</a> country in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the south, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the east, and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west. Angola has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">exclave</a> province, the province of <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda</a> that borders the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> and the Democratic Republic of the Congo. The capital and largest city of Angola is <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>.\n</p><p>Although inhabited since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paleolithic_Era" title="Paleolithic Era">Paleolithic Era</a>, what is now Angola was molded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_Africa" title="Portuguese colonization of Africa">Portuguese colonisation</a>. It began with, and was for centuries limited to, coastal settlements and <a href="/wiki/Trading_post" title="Trading post">trading posts</a> established starting in the 16th century. In the 19th century, European settlers slowly and hesitantly began to establish themselves in the interior. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_West_Africa" title="Portuguese West Africa">Portuguese colony</a> that became Angola did not have its present borders until the early 20th century because of resistance by groups such as the Cuamato, the <a href="/wiki/Oukwanyama" title="Oukwanyama">Kwanyama</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a>.\n</p><p>After a protracted <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">anti-colonial struggle</a>, independence was achieved in 1975 as the <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism&#8211;Leninism">Marxist&#8211;Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Angola" title="People\'s Republic of Angola">People\'s Republic of Angola</a>, a <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a> supported by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war</a> between the ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" title="People\'s Movement for the Liberation of Angola">People\'s Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> (MPLA) and the insurgent anti-communist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Union_for_the_Total_Independence_of_Angola" title="National Union for the Total Independence of Angola">National Union for the Total Independence of Angola</a> (UNITA), supported by the United States and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apartheid_South_Africa" title="Apartheid South Africa">apartheid South Africa</a>, lasted until 2002. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> has since become a relatively stable <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">constitutional republic</a>.\n</p><p>Angola has vast <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mineral_reserve" title="Mineral reserve">mineral</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petroleum_reserves" title="Petroleum reserves">petroleum reserves</a>, and its economy is among the fastest-growing in the world, especially since the end of the civil war; however, the <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a> remains low for most of the population, and <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in Angola is among the lowest in the world, while <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> is among the highest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Angola\'s economic growth is highly uneven, with most of the nation\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wealth_concentration" title="Wealth concentration">wealth concentrated</a> in a disproportionately small sector of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Angola is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>. A highly multiethnic country, Angola\'s 25.8 million people span tribal groups, customs, and traditions. Angolan culture reflects centuries of Portuguese rule, in the predominance of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Angola</i> comes from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> colonial name <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" title="Angola (Portugal)">Reino de Angola</a> (Kingdom of Angola)</i>, which appeared as early as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dias_de_Novais" title="Dias de Novais">Dias de Novais</a>\'s 1571 charter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponym" title="Toponym">toponym</a> was derived by the Portuguese from the title <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Ngolas_of_Ndongo" title="List of Ngolas of Ndongo">ngola</a></i> held by the kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Ndongo</a>. Ndongo in the <a href="/wiki/Highland" title="Highland">highlands</a>, between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kwanza_River" title="Kwanza River">Kwanza</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lukala_River" title="Lukala River">Lukala Rivers</a>, was nominally a possession of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>, but was seeking greater independence in the 16th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Angola" title="History of Angola">History of Angola</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_migrations_and_political_units">Early migrations and political units</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early migrations and political units">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KingdomNdongo1711.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="774" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/KingdomNdongo1711.png/220px-KingdomNdongo1711.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/KingdomNdongo1711.png/330px-KingdomNdongo1711.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/KingdomNdongo1711.png/440px-KingdomNdongo1711.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KingdomNdongo1711.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Territory comprising <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Kingdom of Ndongo</a>, present-day Angola</div></div></div>\n<p>Modern Angola was populated predominantly by <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khoi" title="Khoi">Khoi</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a> prior to the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_migration" title="Bantu migration">Bantu migrations</a>. The Khoi and San peoples were neither <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">pastoralists</a> nor <a href="/wiki/Cultivator" title="Cultivator">cultivators</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henderson_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson-8">[8]</a></sup> They were displaced by <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> arriving from the north, most of whom likely originated in what is today northwestern <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller1_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller1-9">[9]</a></sup> Bantu speakers introduced the cultivation of <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">taro</a>, as well as large cattle herds, to Angola\'s central highlands and the Luanda plain. Hendese Bantu established a number of political entities; the best-known of these was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Kongo" title="Kingdom of the Kongo">Kingdom of the Kongo</a>, based in Angola, which extended northward to what is now the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>. It established <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> with other city-states and civilisations up and down the coast of southwestern and western Africa and even with <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">Great Zimbabwe</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mutapa_Empire" title="Mutapa Empire">Mutapa Empire</a>, although it engaged in little or no transoceanic trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Story_of_Africa_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Story_of_Africa-10">[10]</a></sup> To its south lay the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ndongo" title="Kingdom of Ndongo">Kingdom of Ndongo</a>, from which the area of the later Portuguese colony was sometimes known as <i>Dongo</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_colonisation">Portuguese colonisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Portuguese colonisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Colonial_history_of_Angola" title="Colonial history of Angola">Colonial history of Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese Angola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Loango-Angola" title="Dutch Loango-Angola">Dutch Loango-Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Nzinga_1657.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="953" data-file-width="1438" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/220px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/330px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Queen_Nzinga_1657.png/440px-Queen_Nzinga_1657.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Nzinga_1657.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_Nzinga" title="Queen Nzinga">Queen Nzinga</a> in peace negotiations with the Portuguese governor in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, 1657.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">explorer</a> <a href="/wiki/Diogo_C%C3%A3o" title="Diogo C&#227;o">Diogo C&#227;o</a> reached the area in 1484.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-11">[11]</a></sup> The previous year, the Portuguese had established relations with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a>, which stretched at the time from modern <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> in the north to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kwanza_River" title="Kwanza River">Kwanza River</a> in the south. The Portuguese established their primary early trading post at <a href="/wiki/Soyo" title="Soyo">Soyo</a>, which is now the northernmost city in Angola apart from the <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">exclave</a>. <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Dias_de_Novais" title="Paulo Dias de Novais">Paulo Dias de Novais</a> founded S&#227;o Paulo de Loanda (<a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>) in 1575 with a hundred families of settlers and four hundred soldiers. <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a> was fortified in 1587 and became a township in 1617.\n</p><p>The Portuguese established several other settlements, forts and trading posts along the Angolan coast, principally trading in <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Angola" title="Slavery in Angola">Angolan slaves</a> for <a href="/wiki/Captaincies_of_Brazil" title="Captaincies of Brazil">Brazilian</a> <a href="/wiki/Plantations_in_the_American_South" title="Plantations in the American South">plantations</a>. Local slave dealers provided a large number of slaves for the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fleisch_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fleisch-12">[12]</a></sup> usually in exchange for manufactured goods from Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>This part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a> continued until after <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Brazil" title="Empire of Brazil">Brazil\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence</a> in the 1820s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite Portugal\'s territorial claims in Angola, its control over much of the country\'s vast interior was minimal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-11">[11]</a></sup> In the 16th century Portugal gained control of the coast through a series of treaties and wars. Life for European colonists was difficult and progress slow. <a href="/wiki/John_Iliffe_(historian)" title="John Iliffe (historian)">John Iliffe</a> notes that "Portuguese records of Angola from the 16th century show that a great <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> occurred on average every seventy years; accompanied by epidemic disease, it might kill one-third or one-half of the population, destroying the demographic growth of a generation and forcing colonists back into the river valleys".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kongo_audience.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="491" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kongo_audience.jpg/220px-Kongo_audience.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kongo_audience.jpg/330px-Kongo_audience.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Kongo_audience.jpg/440px-Kongo_audience.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kongo_audience.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An illustration depicting Portuguese encounter with Kongo Royal family.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Loango-Angola" title="Dutch Loango-Angola">occupied</a> the principal settlement of Luanda in 1641, using alliances with local peoples to carry out attacks against Portuguese holdings elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-15">[15]</a></sup> A fleet under <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_S%C3%A1" title="Salvador de S&#225;">Salvador de S&#225;</a> retook Luanda in 1648; reconquest of the rest of the territory was completed by 1650. New treaties with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kongo</a> were signed in 1649; others with <a href="/wiki/Nzinga_of_Ndongo_and_Matamba" title="Nzinga of Ndongo and Matamba">Njinga</a>\'s Kingdom of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matamba" title="Matamba">Matamba</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ndongo" title="Ndongo">Ndongo</a> followed in 1656. The conquest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pungo_Andongo" title="Pungo Andongo">Pungo Andongo</a> in 1671 was the last major Portuguese expansion from Luanda, as attempts to invade Kongo in 1670 and Matamba in 1681 failed. Colonial outposts also expanded inward from Benguela, but until the late 19th century the inroads from Luanda and Benguela were very limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-11">[11]</a></sup> Hamstrung by a series of political upheavals in the early 1800s, Portugal was slow to mount a large scale annexation of Angolan territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-15">[15]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave_trade" title="Slave trade">slave trade</a> was abolished in Angola in 1836, and in 1854 the colonial government freed all its existing slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-15">[15]</a></sup> Four years later, a more progressive administration appointed by Lisbon abolished <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> altogether. However, these decrees remained largely unenforceable, and the Portuguese depended on assistance from the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> to enforce their ban on the slave trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-15">[15]</a></sup> This coincided with a series of renewed military expeditions into the <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a>. By the mid-nineteenth century Portugal had established its dominion as far east as the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> and as far south as <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%A7%C3%A2medes" title="Mo&#231;&#226;medes">Moss&#226;medes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Handbook_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-Handbook-15">[15]</a></sup> Until the late 1880s, Lisbon entertained proposals to link Angola with its <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> but was blocked by British and Belgian opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corrado_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado-17">[17]</a></sup> In this period, the Portuguese came up against different forms of armed resistance from various peoples in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a> in 1884&#8211;1885 set the colony\'s borders, delineating the boundaries of Portuguese claims in Angola,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corrado_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado-17">[17]</a></sup> although many details were unresolved until the 1920s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Trade between Portugal and her African territories also rapidly increased as a result of protective <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a>, leading to increased development, and a wave of new Portuguese immigrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Corrado_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Corrado-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_Angolan_nationalism">Rise of Angolan nationalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rise of Angolan nationalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">Angolan War of Independence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sempreatentos...aoperigo!.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="511" decoding="async" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sempreatentos...aoperigo%21.jpg/220px-Sempreatentos...aoperigo%21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sempreatentos...aoperigo%21.jpg/330px-Sempreatentos...aoperigo%21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sempreatentos...aoperigo%21.jpg/440px-Sempreatentos...aoperigo%21.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sempreatentos...aoperigo!.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portuguese troops on patrol during the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Under colonial law, black Angolans were forbidden from forming political parties or labour unions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okoth_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Okoth-20">[20]</a></sup> The first nationalist movements did not take root until after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, spearheaded by a largely Westernised, Portuguese-speaking urban class which included many <a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mesti&#231;o">mesti&#231;os</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dowden_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dowden-21">[21]</a></sup> During the early 1960s they were joined by other associations stemming from <i>ad hoc</i> labour activism in the rural workforce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okoth_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Okoth-20">[20]</a></sup> Portugal\'s refusal to address increasing Angolan demands for <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a> provoked an armed conflict which erupted in 1961 with the <a href="/wiki/Baixa_de_Cassanje_revolt" title="Baixa de Cassanje revolt">Baixa de Cassanje revolt</a> and gradually evolved into a protracted <a href="/wiki/Angolan_War_of_Independence" title="Angolan War of Independence">war of independence</a> that persisted for the next twelve years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cornwell_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-22">[22]</a></sup> Throughout the conflict, three militant nationalist movements with their own partisan guerrilla wings emerged from the fighting between the Portuguese government and local forces, supported to varying degrees by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Communist_Party" title="Portuguese Communist Party">Portuguese Communist Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dowden_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dowden-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stockwell_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stockwell-23">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FNLA" title="FNLA">National Front for the Liberation of Angola</a></i> (FNLA) recruited from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a> refugees in <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanlon_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hanlon-24">[24]</a></sup> Benefiting from particularly favourable political circumstances in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kinshasha" title="Kinshasha">L&#233;opoldville</a>, and especially from a common border with Zaire, Angolan political exiles were able to build up a power base among a large expatriate community from related families, clans, and traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chabal_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-25">[25]</a></sup> People on both sides of the border spoke mutually intelligible dialects and enjoyed shared ties to the historical Kingdom of Kongo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chabal_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-25">[25]</a></sup> Though as foreigners skilled Angolans could not take advantage of <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu Sese Seko</a>\'s state employment programme, some found work as middlemen for the absentee owners of various lucrative private ventures. The migrants eventually formed the FNLA with the intention of making a bid for political power upon their envisaged return to Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chabal_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A largely <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> guerrilla initiative against the Portuguese in central Angola from 1966 was spearheaded by <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Savimbi" title="Jonas Savimbi">Jonas Savimbi</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/UNITA" title="UNITA">National Union for the Total Independence of Angola</a></i> (UNITA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanlon_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hanlon-24">[24]</a></sup> It remained handicapped by its geographic remoteness from friendly borders, the ethnic fragmentation of the Ovimbundu, and the isolation of peasants on European plantations where they had little opportunity to mobilise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chabal_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-Chabal-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2559" data-file-width="2546" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg/220px-F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg/330px-F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg/440px-F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:F.N.L.A._in_Za%C3%AFre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>FNLA insurgents being trained in <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> in 1973</div></div></div>\n<p>During the late 1950s, the rise of the Marxist&#8211;Leninist <i><a href="/wiki/MPLA" title="MPLA">Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a></i> (MPLA) in the east and Dembos hills north of Luanda came to hold special significance. Formed as a coalition resistance movement by the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Communist_Party" title="Angolan Communist Party">Angolan Communist Party</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cornwell_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-22">[22]</a></sup> the organisation\'s leadership remained predominantly <a href="/wiki/Ambundu" title="Ambundu">Ambundu</a> and courted public sector workers in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanlon_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hanlon-24">[24]</a></sup> Although both the MPLA and its rivals accepted material assistance from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">People\'s Republic of China</a>, the former harboured strong anti-imperialist views and was openly critical of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and its support for Portugal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stockwell_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stockwell-23">[23]</a></sup> This allowed it to win important ground on the diplomatic front, soliciting support from nonaligned governments in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Republic" title="United Arab Republic">United Arab Republic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cornwell_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The MPLA attempted to move its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">Conakry</a> to L&#233;opoldville in October 1961, renewing efforts to create a common front with the FNLA, then known as the <i>Union of Angolan Peoples</i> (UPA) and its leader <a href="/wiki/Holden_Roberto" title="Holden Roberto">Holden Roberto</a>. Roberto turned down the offer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cornwell_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-22">[22]</a></sup> When the MPLA first attempted to insert its own insurgents into Angola, the cadres were ambushed and annihilated by UPA partisans on Roberto\'s orders&#8212;setting a precedent for the bitter factional strife which would later ignite the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cornwell_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-Cornwell-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_war">Civil war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Civil war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Alvor_Agreement" title="Alvor Agreement">Alvor Agreement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuban_intervention_in_Angola" title="Cuban intervention in Angola">Cuban intervention in Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angola_1978.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="736" data-file-width="715" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Angola_1978.jpg/220px-Angola_1978.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Angola_1978.jpg/330px-Angola_1978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Angola_1978.jpg/440px-Angola_1978.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angola_1978.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto" title="Agostinho Neto">Agostinho Neto</a>, MPLA leader and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_state_of_Angola" title="List of heads of state of Angola">Angola\'s first president</a>, meets with Poland\'s ambassador in Luanda, 1978</div></div></div>\n<p>Throughout the war of independence, the three rival nationalist movements were severely hampered by political and military factionalism, as well as their inability to unite guerrilla efforts against the Portuguese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> Between 1961 and 1975 the MPLA, UNITA, and the FNLA competed for influence in the Angolan population and the international community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> became especially sympathetic towards the MPLA and supplied that party with arms, ammunition, funding, and training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> They also backed UNITA militants until it became clear that the latter was at irreconcilable odds with the MPLA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Revolution_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Revolution-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The collapse of Portugal\'s <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> government following the 1974 <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> suspended all Portuguese military activity in Africa and the brokering of a ceasefire pending negotiations for Angolan independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> Encouraged by the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a>, Holden Roberto, Jonas Savimbi, and MPLA chairman <a href="/wiki/Agostinho_Neto" title="Agostinho Neto">Agostinho Neto</a> met in <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> in early January 1975 and agreed to form a coalition government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> This was ratified by the <a href="/wiki/Alvor_Agreement" title="Alvor Agreement">Alvor Agreement</a> later that month, which called for general elections and set the country\'s independence date for 11 November 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> All three factions, however, followed up on the ceasefire by taking advantage of the gradual Portuguese withdrawal to seize various strategic positions, acquire more arms, and enlarge their militant forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> The rapid influx of weapons from numerous external sources, especially the Soviet Union and the United States, as well as the escalation of tensions between the nationalist parties, fueled a new outbreak of hostilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> With tacit American and Zairean support the FNLA began massing large numbers of troops in northern Angola in an attempt to gain military superiority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the MPLA began securing control of Luanda, a traditional Ambundu stronghold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> Sporadic violence broke out in Luanda over the next few months after the FNLA attacked MPLA forces in March 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-4"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> The fighting intensified with street clashes in April and May, and UNITA became involved after over two hundred of its members were massacred by an MPLA contingent that June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-5"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> An upswing in Soviet arms shipments to the MPLA influenced a decision by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> to likewise provide substantial covert aid to the FNLA and UNITA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 1975, the MPLA requested direct assistance from the Soviet Union in the form of ground troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-29">[29]</a></sup> The Soviets declined, offering to send advisers but no troops; however, Cuba was more forthcoming and in late September dispatched nearly five hundred combat personnel to Angola, along with sophisticated weaponry and supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Revolution_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Revolution-27">[27]</a></sup> By independence there were over a thousand Cuban soldiers in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-29">[29]</a></sup> They were kept supplied by a massive <a href="/wiki/Cuba%E2%80%93Angola_airbridge" title="Cuba&#8211;Angola airbridge">airbridge</a> carried out with Soviet aircraft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-29">[29]</a></sup> The persistent buildup of Cuban and Soviet military aid allowed the MPLA to drive its opponents from Luanda and blunt an abortive intervention by Zairean and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South African</a> troops, which had deployed in a belated attempt to assist the FNLA and UNITA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weigert_28-6"><a href="#cite_note-Weigert-28">[28]</a></sup> The FNLA was largely annihilated, although UNITA managed to withdraw its civil officials and militia from Luanda and seek sanctuary in the southern provinces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rothschild1_26-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rothschild1-26">[26]</a></sup> From there, Savimbi continued to mount a determined insurgent campaign against the MPLA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vanneman_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-Vanneman-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FAPLA_car_burning.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="573" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/FAPLA_car_burning.PNG/220px-FAPLA_car_burning.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/FAPLA_car_burning.PNG/330px-FAPLA_car_burning.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/FAPLA_car_burning.PNG/440px-FAPLA_car_burning.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FAPLA_car_burning.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An MPLA staff car burns after being destroyed in the fighting outside Novo Redondo (present-day <a href="/wiki/Sumbe" title="Sumbe">Sumbe</a>) in late 1975.</div></div></div>\n<p>Between 1975 and 1991, the MPLA implemented an economic and political system based on the principles of <a href="/wiki/Scientific_socialism" title="Scientific socialism">scientific socialism</a>, incorporating <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">central planning</a> and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" title="Marxist&#8211;Leninist">Marxist&#8211;Leninist</a> <a href="/wiki/One-party_state" title="One-party state">one-party state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arming_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-30">[30]</a></sup> It embarked on an ambitious programme of <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalisation</a>, and the domestic private sector was essentially abolished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arming_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-30">[30]</a></sup> Privately owned enterprises were nationalised and incorporated into a single umbrella of state-owned enterprises known as <i>Unidades Economicas Estatais</i> (UEE).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arming_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-30">[30]</a></sup> Under the MPLA, Angola experienced a significant degree of modern <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arming_30-3"><a href="#cite_note-Arming-30">[30]</a></sup> However, corruption and graft also increased and public resources were either allocated inefficiently or simply embezzled by officials for personal enrichment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SSG1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-SSG1-31">[31]</a></sup> The ruling party survived an attempted coup d\'&#233;tat by the <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoist</a>-oriented <a href="/wiki/Communist_Organization_of_Angola" title="Communist Organization of Angola">Communist Organisation of Angola</a> (OCA) in 1977, which was suppressed after a series of bloody political purges left thousands of OCA supporters dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker1_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker1-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The MPLA abandoned its former Marxist ideology at its third party congress in 1990, and declared <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a> to be its new platform.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tucker1_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker1-32">[32]</a></sup> Angola subsequently became a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>; restrictions on the market economy were also reduced in an attempt to draw foreign investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tordoff1_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tordoff1-33">[33]</a></sup> By May 1991 it reached a peace agreement with UNITA, the <a href="/wiki/Bicesse_Accords" title="Bicesse Accords">Bicesse Accords</a>, which scheduled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angolan_general_election,_1992" title="Angolan general election, 1992">new general elections</a> for September 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tordoff1_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tordoff1-33">[33]</a></sup> When the MPLA secured a major electoral victory, UNITA objected to the results of both the presidential and legislative vote count and returned to war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tordoff1_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tordoff1-33">[33]</a></sup> Following the election, the <a href="/wiki/Halloween_massacre_(Angola)" title="Halloween massacre (Angola)">Halloween massacre</a> occurred from 30 October to 1 November, where MPLA forces killed thousands of UNITA supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceasefire_with_UNITA">Ceasefire with UNITA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ceasefire with UNITA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2000s_in_Angola" title="2000s in Angola">2000s in Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cabinda,_R._Congo,_D.R._Congo,_Angola.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="380" decoding="async" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png/220px-Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png/330px-Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/Cabinda%2C_R._Congo%2C_D.R._Congo%2C_Angola.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cabinda,_R._Congo,_D.R._Congo,_Angola.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Cabinda_Province" title="Cabinda Province">Cabinda Province</a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00ff00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Republic of the Congo</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Democratic Republic of the Congo</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff00ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;The rest of Angola</div></div></div></div>\n<p>On 22 March 2002, Jonas Savimbi was killed in action against government troops. UNITA and the MPLA reached a cease-fire shortly afterwards. UNITA gave up its armed wing and assumed the role of a major opposition party. Although the political situation of the country began to stabilise, regular democratic processes did not prevail until the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Angola" title="Elections in Angola">elections in Angola</a> in 2008 and 2012 and the adoption of a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">constitution</a> in 2010, all of which strengthened the prevailing <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant-party system</a>.\n</p><p>Angola has a serious humanitarian crisis; the result of the prolonged war, of the abundance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minefield" title="Minefield">minefields</a>, of the continued political (and to a much lesser degree) military activities in favour of the independence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a> (carried out in the context of the protracted <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_War" title="Cabinda War">Cabinda conflict</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">FLEC</a>), but most of all, by the depredation of the country\'s rich mineral resources by the r&#233;gime.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While most of the internally displaced have now settled around the capital, in the so-called <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/musseque" title="wikt:musseque">musseques</a></i>, the general situation for Angolans remains desperate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">Drought</a> in 2016 caused the worst food crisis in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a> in 25 years. Drought affected 1.4 million people across seven of Angola\'s 18 provinces. Food prices rose and acute <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> rates doubled, with more than 95,000 children affected. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_insecurity" title="Food insecurity">Food insecurity</a> was expected<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (December 2016)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to worsen from July to December 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Angola" title="Geography of Angola">Geography of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela,_Angola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/220px-Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/330px-Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/440px-Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beach_of_Coatinha_in_Benguela,_Angola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Miradouro da Lua on the south coast of <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Epupa_Falls_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Epupa_Falls_2.jpg/220px-Epupa_Falls_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Epupa_Falls_2.jpg/330px-Epupa_Falls_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Epupa_Falls_2.jpg/440px-Epupa_Falls_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Epupa_Falls_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Epupa_Falls" title="Epupa Falls">Epupa Falls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cunene_River" title="Cunene River">Cunene River</a> on the border of Angola and <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG/220px-Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG/330px-Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG/440px-Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_Stones_Pungo_Adongo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Black_Rocks_at_Pungo_Andongo" title="Black Rocks at Pungo Andongo">Black Rocks at Pungo Andongo</a> near Malange.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Topography.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1387" data-file-width="1318" decoding="async" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Angola_Topography.png/220px-Angola_Topography.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Angola_Topography.png/330px-Angola_Topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Angola_Topography.png/440px-Angola_Topography.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Topography.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Angola.</div></div></div>\n<p>At 1,246,620&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (481,321&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Angola is the world\'s twenty-third largest country - comparable in size to Mali, or twice the size of France or of Texas. It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_south" title="4th parallel south">4&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_south" title="18th parallel south">18&#176;S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/24th_meridian_east" title="24th meridian east">24&#176;E</a>.\n</p><p>Angola borders <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the north-east and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_Ocean" title="South Atlantic Ocean">South Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west. The coastal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a> in the north has borders with the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the north and with the Democratic Republic of the Congo to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>\nAngola\'s capital, <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, lies on the Atlantic coast in the northwest of the country.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Angola" title="Climate of Angola">Climate of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1311" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_AGO_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>K&#246;ppen-Geiger climate classification map for Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Angola, although located in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_zone" title="Tropical zone">tropical zone</a>, has a climate that is not characterized for this region, due to the confluence of three factors:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Benguela_Current" title="Benguela Current">Benguela Current</a>, cold, along the southern part of the coast;</li>\n<li>The relief in the interior;</li>\n<li>Influence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Namib_Desert" title="Namib Desert">Namib Desert</a> in the southwest.</li></ul>\n<p>As a result, Angola\'s climate is characterized by two seasons: rainfall from October to April and drought, known as <i>Cacimbo</i>, from May to August, drier, as the name implies, and with lower temperatures. On the other hand, while the coastline has high rainfall rates, decreasing from North to South and from 800 millimetres (31 inches) to 50 millimetres (2.0 inches), with average annual temperatures above 23&#160;&#176;C (73&#160;&#176;F), the interior zone can be divided into three areas:\n</p>\n<ul><li>North, with high rainfall and high temperatures;</li>\n<li>Central Plateau, with a dry season and average temperatures of the order of 19&#160;&#176;C;</li>\n<li>South with very high thermal amplitudes due to the proximity of the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a> and the influence of masses of tropical air.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Angola" title="Politics of Angola">Politics of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Angola" title="Elections in Angola">Elections in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Angola" title="List of political parties in Angola">List of political parties in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Angola" title="Foreign relations of Angola">Foreign relations of Angola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Angola" title="List of diplomatic missions of Angola">List of diplomatic missions of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Jose_Eduardo_dos_Santos-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos" title="Jos&#233; Eduardo dos Santos">Jos&#233; Eduardo dos Santos</a> meets with <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> (2006).</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angola_National_Assembly_Building_(19898889148).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Angola_National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg/220px-Angola_National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Angola_National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg/330px-Angola_National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Angola_National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg/440px-Angola_National_Assembly_Building_%2819898889148%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angola_National_Assembly_Building_(19898889148).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The National Assembly building in Luanda was built by a Portuguese company in 2013 at a cost of US$185 million</div></div></div>\n<p>The Angolan government is composed of three branches of government: executive, legislative and judicial. The executive branch of the government is composed of the President, the Vice-Presidents and the Council of Ministers. The legislative branch comprises a 220-seat <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislature elected from both provincial and nationwide constituencies. For decades, political power has been concentrated in the presidency.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">Constitution of 2010</a> establishes the broad outlines of government structure and delineates the rights and duties of citizens. The legal system is based on Portuguese law and customary law but is weak and fragmented, and courts operate in only 12 of more than 140 municipalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> A Supreme Court serves as the appellate tribunal; a Constitutional Court does not hold the powers of <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review" title="Judicial review">judicial review</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-44">[44]</a></sup> Governors of the 18 provinces are appointed by the president.\n</p><p>After the end of the civil war the regime came under pressure from within as well as from the international community to become more democratic and less authoritarian. Its reaction was to implement a number of changes without substantially changing its character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Angola is classified as \'not free\' by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> 2014 report.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-46">[46]</a></sup> The report noted that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angolan_legislative_election,_2012" title="Angolan legislative election, 2012">August 2012 parliamentary elections</a>, in which the ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Popular_Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Angola" title="Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola">Popular Movement for the Liberation of Angola</a> won more than 70% of the vote, suffered from serious flaws, including outdated and inaccurate voter rolls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-46">[46]</a></sup> Voter turnout dropped from 80% in 2008 to 60%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Angola scored poorly on the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>. It was ranked 39 out of 52 <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan African</a> countries, scoring particularly badly in the areas of participation and human rights, sustainable economic opportunity and human development. The Ibrahim Index uses a number of variables to compile its list which reflects the state of governance in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1978" data-file-width="1140" decoding="async" height="382" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg/220px-Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg/330px-Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg/440px-Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Eduardo_dos_Santos" title="Jos&#233; Eduardo dos Santos">Jos&#233; Eduardo dos Santos</a>, second President of Angola from 1979 to 2017.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Angola" title="Constitution of Angola">new constitution</a>, adopted in 2010, did away with presidential elections, introducing a system in which the president and the vice-president of the political party that wins the parliamentary elections automatically become president and vice-president. Directly or indirectly, the president controls all other organs of the state, so there is <i>de facto</i> no <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In the classifications used in constitutional law, this government falls under the category of <i>authoritarian regime.</i> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 October 2014, Angola was elected for the second time as a non-permanent member of the UN Security Council, with 190 favourable votes out of 193. The mandate began on 1 January 2015 and lasts for two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also that month, the country took on the leadership of the African ministers and governors at the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, following debates at the annual meetings of both entities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since January 2014 the Republic of Angola has held the rotating presidency of the <a href="/wiki/International_Conference_on_the_Great_Lakes_Region" title="International Conference on the Great Lakes Region">International Conference on the Great Lakes Region</a> (ICGLR).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In 2015, the executive secretary of ICGLR, <a href="/wiki/Ntumba_Luaba" title="Ntumba Luaba">Ntumba Luaba</a>, called Angola an example to be followed because of the significant progress it made over the 12 years of peace, particularly in terms of socioeconomic and political-military stability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After 38 years of rule, in 2017 President dos Santos stepped down from MPLA leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The leader of the winning party at the parliamentary elections in August 2017 would become the next president of Angola. The MPLA selected Defense Minister General <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Louren%C3%A7o" title="Jo&#227;o Louren&#231;o">Jo&#227;o Louren&#231;o</a> and won the election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In what has been described as a political purge<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2017)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to cement his power and reduce the influence of the Dos Santos family, Louren&#231;o subsequently sacked the chief of the national police, Ambr&#243;sio de Lemos, and the head of the intelligence service, Apolin&#225;rio Jos&#233; Pereira. Both are considered allies of former president Dos Santos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> He also removed <a href="/wiki/Isabel_dos_Santos" title="Isabel dos Santos">Isabel Dos Santos</a>, daughter of the former president, as head of the country\'s state oil company Sonangol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Armed_Forces" title="Angolan Armed Forces">Angolan Armed Forces</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="722" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg/220px-Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg/330px-Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg/440px-Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angolan_Air_Force_Ilyushin_Il-76TD_Karpezo-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Angolan Air Force Ilyushin Il-76TD Karpezo-1</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="719" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png/220px-Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png/330px-Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png/440px-Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angolan_soldiers_training_in_Russia.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angolan_Army" title="Angolan Army">Angolan Army</a> training in Russia. From left to right, the ranks of the men are Second Lieutenant, First Lieutenant, and Captain.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Angolan Armed Forces (AAF) are headed by a Chief of Staff who reports to the Minister of Defence. There are three divisions&#8212;the Army (Ex&#233;rcito), Navy (Marinha de Guerra, MGA) and <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Force_of_Angola" title="National Air Force of Angola">National Air Force</a> (For&#231;a A&#233;rea Nacional, FAN). Total manpower is about 110,000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Its equipment includes Russian-manufactured fighters, bombers and transport planes. There are also Brazilian-made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EMB-312_Tucano" title="EMB-312 Tucano">EMB-312 Tucanos</a> for training, Czech-made L-39s for training and bombing, and a variety of western-made aircraft such as the C-212\\Aviocar, Sud Aviation Alouette III, etc. A small number of AAF personnel are stationed in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (Kinshasa) and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> (Brazzaville).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police">Police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The National Police departments are Public Order, Criminal Investigation, Traffic and Transport, Investigation and Inspection of Economic Activities, Taxation and Frontier Supervision, Riot Police and the Rapid Intervention Police. The National Police are in the process of standing up an air wing,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (November 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> to provide helicopter support for operations. The National Police are developing their criminal investigation and forensic capabilities. The force has an estimated 6,000 patrol officers, 2,500 taxation and frontier supervision officers, 182 criminal investigators and 100 financial crimes detectives and around 90 economic activity inspectors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The National Police have implemented a modernisation and development plan to increase the capabilities and efficiency of the total force.
