In addition to administrative reorganisation, modernisation projects include procurement of new vehicles, aircraft and equipment, construction of new police stations and forensic laboratories, restructured training programmes and the replacement of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AKM_rifle" title="AKM rifle">AKM rifles</a> with 9&#160;mm <a href="/wiki/Uzi" title="Uzi">Uzis</a> for officers in urban areas.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Justice">Justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A Supreme Court serves as a court of appeal. The Constitutional Court is the supreme body of the constitutional jurisdiction, established with the approval of Law no. 2/08, of 17 June &#8211; Organic Law of the Constitutional Court and Law n. 3/08, of 17 June &#8211; Organic Law of the Constitutional Process. The legal system is based on Portuguese and customary laws, but it is weak and fragmented. There are only 12 courts in more than 140 counties in the country. Its first task was the validation of the candidacies of the political parties to the legislative elections of 5 September 2008. Thus, on 25 June 2008, the Constitutional Court was institutionalized and its Judicial Counselors assumed the position before the President of the Republic. Currently, seven advisory judges are present, four men and three women.\n</p><p>In 2014, a new penal code took effect in Angola. The classification of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Money-laundering" title="Money-laundering">money-laundering</a> as a crime is one of the novelties in the new legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG/250px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG/375px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG/500px-Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diplomatic_missions_of_Angola.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Diplomatic missions of Angola.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 16 October 2014, Angola was elected for the second time a non-permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, with 190 favorable votes out of a total of 193. The term of office began on 1 January 2015 and expired on 31 December 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since January 2014, the Republic of Angola has been chairing the International Conference for the Great Lakes Region (CIRGL). [80] In 2015, CIRGL Executive Secretary Ntumba Luaba said that Angola is the example to be followed by the members of the organization, due to the significant progress made during the 12 years of peace, namely in terms of socio-economic stability and political- military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Angola" title="Human rights in Angola">Human rights in Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Angola" title="LGBT rights in Angola">LGBT rights in Angola</a></div>\n<p>In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexual</a> acts were decriminalized in Angola, and the government also prohibited discrimination based on sexual orientation. The vote was overwhelming: 155 for, 1 against, 7 abstaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Angola" title="Provinces of Angola">Provinces of Angola</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Angola" title="Municipalities of Angola">Municipalities of Angola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Angola" title="Communes of Angola">Communes of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png/220px-Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Provinces_numbered_300px.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Angola with the provinces numbered</div></div></div>\n<p>As of  March 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Angola is divided into <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Angola" title="Provinces of Angola">eighteen provinces</a> (<i>prov&#237;ncias</i>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Angola" title="Municipalities of Angola">162 municipalities</a>. The municipalities are further divided into 559 communes (townships).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-acd_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-acd-63">[63]</a></sup> The provinces are:\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ol><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengo_(province)" title="Bengo (province)">Bengo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Benguela_Province" title="Benguela Province">Benguela</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bi%C3%A9_(province)" title="Bi&#233; (province)">Bi&#233;</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuando_Cubango" title="Cuando Cubango">Cuando Cubango</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuanza_Norte" title="Cuanza Norte">Cuanza Norte</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuanza_Sul" title="Cuanza Sul">Cuanza Sul</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cunene_(province)" title="Cunene (province)">Cunene</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Huambo_Province" title="Huambo Province">Huambo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hu%C3%ADla_Province" title="Hu&#237;la Province">Hu&#237;la</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Luanda_Province" title="Luanda Province">Luanda</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunda_Norte" title="Lunda Norte">Lunda Norte</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunda_Sul" title="Lunda Sul">Lunda Sul</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Malanje_Province" title="Malanje Province">Malanje</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moxico_(province)" title="Moxico (province)">Moxico</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Namibe_Province" title="Namibe Province">Namibe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/U%C3%ADge_Province" title="U&#237;ge Province">U&#237;ge</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Zaire_Province" title="Zaire Province">Zaire</a></li></ol></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Exclave_of_Cabinda">Exclave of Cabinda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Exclave of Cabinda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabinda_(province)" title="Cabinda (province)">Cabinda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Cabinda" title="Republic of Cabinda">Republic of Cabinda</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cabinda_(FLEC_propose).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Flag_of_Cabinda_%28FLEC_propose%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Cabinda_%28FLEC_propose%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Flag_of_Cabinda_%28FLEC_propose%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Cabinda_%28FLEC_propose%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Flag_of_Cabinda_%28FLEC_propose%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Cabinda_%28FLEC_propose%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Cabinda_(FLEC_propose).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda (FLEC)</a></div></div></div>\n<p>With an area of approximately 7,283 square kilometres (2,812&#160;sq&#160;mi), the Northern Angolan province of Cabinda is unusual in being separated from the rest of the country by a strip, some 60 kilometres (37&#160;mi) wide, of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> along the lower <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>. Cabinda borders the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Republic" title="Congo Republic">Congo Republic</a> to the north and north-northeast and the DRC to the east and south. The town of Cabinda is the chief population centre.\n</p><p>According to a 1995 census, Cabinda had an estimated population of 600,000, approximately 400,000 of whom live in neighbouring countries. Population estimates are, however, highly unreliable. Consisting largely of tropical forest, Cabinda produces hardwoods, coffee, cocoa, crude rubber and palm oil. The product for which it is best known, however, is its oil, which has given it the nickname, "the Kuwait of Africa". Cabinda\'s petroleum production from its considerable offshore reserves now accounts for more than half of Angola\'s output.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Most of the oil along its coast was discovered under <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Portuguese rule</a> by the Cabinda Gulf Oil Company (CABGOC) from 1968 onwards.\n</p><p>Ever since <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> handed over sovereignty of its former overseas province of Angola to the local independence groups (MPLA, UNITA and FNLA), the territory of Cabinda has been a focus of separatist guerrilla actions opposing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Angola" title="Government of Angola">Government of Angola</a> (which has employed its armed forces, the FAA&#8212;For&#231;as Armadas Angolanas) and Cabindan separatists. The <a href="/wiki/Front_for_the_Liberation_of_the_Enclave_of_Cabinda" title="Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda">Front for the Liberation of the Enclave of Cabinda</a>-<a href="/wiki/For%C3%A7as_Armadas_de_Cabinda" title="For&#231;as Armadas de Cabinda">Armed Forces of Cabinda</a> (FLEC-FAC) announced a virtual Federal Republic of Cabinda under the Presidency of N\'Zita Henriques Tiago. One of the characteristics of the Cabindan independence movement is its constant fragmentation, into smaller and smaller factions.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Angola" title="Economy of Angola">Economy of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_(8222830479).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg/220px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg/330px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg/440px-First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_%288222830479%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_WAFMAX_in_Angola_3_(8222830479).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A booming economy due to oil revenues and stable politics, Angola has seen an increase in its international trading sector.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luanda-Sonangol.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="267" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luanda-Sonangol.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luanda city centre.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/330px-Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg/440px-Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banco_Nacional_de_Angola_in_Luanda_-_Angola_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Banco Nacional de Angola building on the Marginal in Luanda dates from 1956.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-357M,_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Boeing_747-357M%2C_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg/220px-Boeing_747-357M%2C_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Boeing_747-357M%2C_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg/330px-Boeing_747-357M%2C_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Boeing_747-357M%2C_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg/440px-Boeing_747-357M%2C_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-357M,_TAAG_Angola_Airlines_AN0387063.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TAAG_Angolan_Airlines" title="TAAG Angolan Airlines">TAAG Angolan Airlines</a> is Angola\'s national airline.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_housing_development_area.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/New_housing_development_area.jpg/220px-New_housing_development_area.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/New_housing_development_area.jpg/330px-New_housing_development_area.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/New_housing_development_area.jpg/440px-New_housing_development_area.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_housing_development_area.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New suburb (new housing area) in Luanda built in 2010.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination,_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1351" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG/220px-Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG/330px-Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG/440px-Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination%2C_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Offshore_platform_on_move_to_final_destination,_Ilha_de_Luanda.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Offshore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petrol" title="Petrol">petrol</a> platform prepared for moving to final destination on high sea, Luanda, Angola, Atlantic Ocean</div></div></div>\n<p>Angola has diamonds, oil, gold, copper and a rich wildlife (dramatically impoverished during the civil war), forest and fossil fuels. Since independence, oil and diamonds have been the most important economic resource. Smallholder and <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantation</a> agriculture dramatically dropped in the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a>, but began to recover after 2002. The transformation industry<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> of the late colonial period collapsed at independence, because of the exodus of most of the ethnic Portuguese population, but it has begun to re-emerge with updated technologies, partly because of an influx of new Portuguese entrepreneurs. Similar developments have taken place in the service sector.\n</p><p>Angola\'s economy has in recent years moved on from the disarray caused by a quarter-century of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angolan_civil_war" title="Angolan civil war">Angolan civil war</a> to become the fastest-growing economy in Africa and one of the fastest-growing in the world, with an average <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> growth of 20% between 2005 and 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In the period 2001&#8211;10, Angola had the world\'s highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_average_GDP_growth" title="Annual average GDP growth">annual average GDP growth</a>, at 11.1%.\n</p><p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Exim_Bank_of_China" title="Exim Bank of China">Exim Bank of China</a> approved a $2&#160;billion <a href="/wiki/Line_of_credit" title="Line of credit">line of credit</a> to Angola, to be used for rebuilding Angola\'s <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure" title="Infrastructure">infrastructure</a>, and to limit the influence of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>China is Angola\'s biggest trade partner and <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">export</a> destination as well as the fourth-largest source of <a href="/wiki/Import" title="Import">imports</a>. Bilateral trade reached $27.67&#160;billion in 2011, up 11.5% year-on-year. China\'s imports, mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> and diamonds, increased 9.1% to $24.89&#160;billion while China\'s exports to Angola, including mechanical and electrical products, machinery parts and construction materials, surged 38.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The oil <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">glut</a> led to a local <a href="/wiki/Price" title="Price">price</a> for unleaded gasoline of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">&#163;</a>0.37 a gallon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> reported in 2008 that diamonds and oil make up 60% of Angola\'s economy, almost all of the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Revenue" title="Revenue">revenue</a> and all of its dominant <a href="/wiki/Export" title="Export">exports</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Growth is almost entirely driven by rising <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">oil production</a> which surpassed 1.4 million barrels per day (220,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) in late 2005 and was expected to grow to 2 million barrels per day (320,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>/d) by 2007. Control of the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil industry</a> is consolidated in <a href="/wiki/Sonangol_Group" title="Sonangol Group">Sonangol Group</a>, a conglomerate owned by the Angolan government. In December 2006, Angola was admitted as a member of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Operations in its <a href="/wiki/List_of_diamond_mines" title="List of diamond mines">diamond mines</a> include partnerships between state-run <a href="/wiki/Endiama" title="Endiama">Endiama</a> and mining companies such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ALROSA" title="ALROSA">ALROSA</a> which operate in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Angolan economy grew 18% in 2005, 26% in 2006 and 17.6% in 2007. Due to the global <a href="/wiki/Recession" title="Recession">recession</a> the economy contracted an estimated &#8722;0.3% in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-44">[44]</a></sup> The security brought about by the 2002 peace settlement has allowed the resettlement of 4&#160;million displaced persons and a resulting large-scale increases in agriculture production.\n</p><p>Although the country\'s economy has grown significantly since Angola achieved political stability in 2002, mainly due to fast-rising earnings in the oil sector, Angola faces huge social and economic problems. These are in part a result of almost continual armed conflict from 1961 on, although the highest level of destruction and socio-economic damage took place after the 1975 independence, during the long years of <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war</a>. However, high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_rate" title="Poverty rate">poverty rates</a> and blatant <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">social inequality</a> chiefly stem from persistent <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a>, "neo-patrimonial" practices at all levels of the political, administrative, military and economic structures, and of <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Angola" title="Corruption in Angola">a pervasive corruption</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The main beneficiaries are political, administrative, economic and military power holders, who have accumulated (and continue to accumulate) enormous wealth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>\n</p><p>"Secondary beneficiaries" are the middle strata which are about to become <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social classes</a>. However, almost half the population has to be considered poor, with dramatic differences between the countryside and the cities (where by now slightly more than 50% of the people live).\n</p><p>A study carried out in 2008 by the Angolan Instituto Nacional de Estat&#237;stica found that in rural areas roughly 58% must be classified as "poor" according to UN norms, but in the urban areas only 19%, and an overall rate of 37%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In cities, a majority of families, well beyond those officially classified as poor, must adopt a variety of survival strategies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In urban areas social inequality is most evident and it\'s extreme in Luanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> Angola constantly ranks in the bottom group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">the Heritage Foundation</a>, a conservative American <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a>, oil production from Angola has increased so significantly that Angola now is China\'s biggest supplier of oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> "China has extended three multibillion dollar lines of credit to the Angolan government; two loans of $2 billion from China Exim Bank, one in 2004, the second in 2007, as well as one loan in 2005 of $2.9 billion from <a href="/wiki/China_International_Fund" title="China International Fund">China International Fund</a> Ltd."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Growing oil revenues also created opportunities for <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Angola" title="Corruption in Angola">corruption</a>: according to a recent <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> report, 32&#160;billion US dollars disappeared from government accounts in 2007&#8211;2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Furthermore, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonangol" title="Sonangol">Sonangol</a>, the state-run oil company, controls 51% of Cabinda\'s oil. Due to this market control the company ends up determining the profit received by the government and the taxes it pays. The council of foreign affairs states that the World Bank mentioned that Sonangol " is a taxpayer, it carries out quasi-fiscal activities, it invests public funds, and, as concessionaire, it is a sector regulator. This multifarious work programme creates conflicts of interest and characterises a complex relationship between Sonangol and the government that weakens the formal budgetary process and creates uncertainty as regards the actual fiscal stance of the state."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before independence in 1975, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" title="Angola (Portugal)">Angola</a> was a breadbasket of southern Africa and a major exporter of <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, coffee and <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">three decades of civil war</a> (1975&#8211;2002) destroyed fertile countryside, left it littered with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landmine" title="Landmine">landmines</a> and drove millions into the cities. The country now depends on expensive food imports, mainly from South Africa and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, while more than 90% of farming is done at the family and subsistence level. Thousands of Angolan small-scale farmers are trapped in poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The enormous differences between the regions pose a serious structural problem for the Angolan economy, illustrated by the fact that about one third of economic activities are concentrated in Luanda and neighbouring Bengo province, while several areas of the interior suffer economic stagnation and even regression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p><p>One of the economic consequences of the social and regional disparities is a sharp increase in Angolan private investments abroad. The small fringe of Angolan society where most of the asset accumulation takes place seeks to spread its assets, for reasons of security and profit. For the time being, the biggest share of these investments is concentrated in Portugal where the <a href="/wiki/Angolans_in_Portugal" title="Angolans in Portugal">Angolan presence</a> (including the family of the state president) in banks as well as in the domains of energy, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Angola" title="Telecommunications in Angola">telecommunications</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">mass media</a> has become notable, as has the acquisition of vineyards and orchards as well as of touristic enterprises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> nations are globally achieving impressive improvements in well-being, according to a report by <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>\'s Africa Governance Initiative and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Boston_Consulting_Group" title="The Boston Consulting Group">the Boston Consulting Group</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Angola has upgraded critical infrastructure, an investment made possible by funds from the nation\'s development of oil resources. According to this report, just slightly more than ten years after the end of the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">civil war</a> Angola\'s standard of living has overall greatly improved. Life expectancy, which was just 46 years in 2002, reached 51 in 2011. Mortality rates for children fell from 25 percent in 2001 to 19 percent in 2010 and the number of students enrolled in primary school has tripled since 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> However, at the same time the social and economic inequality that has characterised the country since long has not diminished, but on the contrary deepened in all respects.\n</p><p>With a stock of assets corresponding to 70&#160;billion Kz (US$6.8&#160;billion), Angola is now the third largest financial market in sub-Saharan Africa, surpassed only by <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and South Africa. According to the Angolan Minister of Economy, Abra&#227;o Gourgel, the financial market of the country grew modestly from 2002 and now lies in third place at the level of sub-Saharan Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Angola\'s economy is expected to grow by 3.9 percent in 2014 said the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), robust growth in the non-oil economy, mainly driven by a very good performance in the agricultural sector, is expected to offset a temporary drop in oil production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Angola\'s financial system is maintained by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Angola" title="National Bank of Angola">National Bank of Angola</a> and managed by governor <a class="extiw" href="https://no.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jose_de_Lima_Massano" title="no:Jose de Lima Massano">Jose de Lima Massano</a>. According to a study on the banking sector, carried out by <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, the monetary policy led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banco_Nacional_de_Angola" title="Banco Nacional de Angola">Banco Nacional de Angola</a> (BNA), the Angolan national bank, allowed a decrease in the inflation rate put at 7.96% in December 2013, which contributed to the sector\'s growth trend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Estimates released by Angola\'s central bank, said country\'s economy should grow at an annual average rate of 5 percent over the next four years, boosted by the increasing participation of the private sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 December 2014, the Capital Market in Angola started. <a href="/wiki/Angola_Stock_Exchange" title="Angola Stock Exchange">BODIVA</a> (Angola Securities and Debt Stock Exchange, in English) received the secondary public debt market, and it is expected to start the corporate debt market by 2015, but the stock market should be a reality only in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Angola" title="Agriculture in Angola">Agriculture in Angola</a></div>\n<p>Agriculture and forestry is an area of potential opportunity for the country. The African Economic Outlook organization states that "Angola requires 4.5 million tonnes a year of grain but grows only about 55% of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corn" title="Corn">corn</a> it needs, 20% of the <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and just 5% of its required <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In addition, the World Bank estimates that "less than 3 percent of Angola\'s abundant fertile land is cultivated and the economic potential of the forestry sector remains largely unexploited" .<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" title="Transport in Angola">Transport in Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG/440px-Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aeroport-4-de-Fevereiro-Chegadas_LWS1962.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luanda_Airport" title="Luanda Airport">Quatro de Fevereiro Luanda Airport</a> arrivals.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Benguela_Railway_Station_(19603443258).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Benguela_Railway_Station_%2819603443258%29.jpg/220px-Benguela_Railway_Station_%2819603443258%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Benguela_Railway_Station_%2819603443258%29.jpg/330px-Benguela_Railway_Station_%2819603443258%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Benguela_Railway_Station_%2819603443258%29.jpg/440px-Benguela_Railway_Station_%2819603443258%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Benguela_Railway_Station_(19603443258).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Train station in <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cargamento_de_mineirios,_Namibe.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cargamento_de_mineirios%2C_Namibe.JPG/220px-Cargamento_de_mineirios%2C_Namibe.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cargamento_de_mineirios%2C_Namibe.JPG/330px-Cargamento_de_mineirios%2C_Namibe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Cargamento_de_mineirios%2C_Namibe.JPG/440px-Cargamento_de_mineirios%2C_Namibe.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cargamento_de_mineirios,_Namibe.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ship loading minerals at Namibe harbour, Angola.</div></div></div>\n<p>Transport in Angola consists of:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Three separate <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Angola" title="Rail transport in Angola">railway systems</a> totalling 2,761&#160;km (1,716&#160;mi)</li>\n<li>76,626&#160;km (47,613&#160;mi) of highway of which 19,156&#160;km (11,903&#160;mi) is paved</li>\n<li>1,295 navigable inland waterways</li>\n<li>Eight major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_port" title="Sea port">sea ports</a></li>\n<li>243 <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Angola" title="List of airports in Angola">airports</a>, of which 32 are paved.</li></ul>\n<p>Travel on highways outside of towns and cities in Angola (and in some cases within) is often not best advised for those without four-by-four vehicles. While a reasonable road infrastructure has existed within Angola, time and the war have taken their toll on the road surfaces, leaving many severely potholed, littered with broken asphalt. In many areas drivers have established alternate tracks to avoid the worst parts of the surface, although careful attention must be paid to the presence or absence of landmine warning markers by the side of the road. The Angolan government has contracted the restoration of many of the country\'s roads. The road between Lubango and Namibe, for example, was completed recently with funding from the European Union, and is comparable to many European main routes. Completing the road infrastructure is likely to take some decades, but substantial efforts are already being made.\n</p><p>Transport is an important aspect in Angola because it is strategically located and it could become a regional logistics hub. In addition Angola has some of the most important and biggest ports and so it is vital to connect them to the interior of the country as well as to neighbouring countries.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Angola" title="Tourism in Angola">Tourism</a> is restarting on the heels of the long ended stop in the civil war, and very few tourists venture anywhere in Angola yet due to lack of infrastructure.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunications</a> industry is considered one of the main strategic sectors in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2014, the building of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optic_fiber" title="Optic fiber">optic fiber</a> underwater cable was announced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> This project aims to turn Angola into a continental hub, thus improving Internet connections both nationally and internationally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 March 2015, the First Angolan Forum of Telecommunications and Information Technology was held in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a> under the motto "The challenges of telecommunications in the current context of Angola",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> to promote debate on topical issues on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> in Angola and worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> A study of this sector, presented at the forum, said Angola had the first telecommunications operator in Africa to test LTE &#8211; with speeds up to 400 Mbit/s &#8211; and mobile penetration of about 75%; there are about 3.5 million <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> in the Angolan market; There are about 25,000 kilometres (16,000 miles) of optical fibre installed in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Angolan <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angosat_1" title="Angosat 1">AngoSat-1</a>, was launched into orbit on 26 December 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> It was launched from the <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">Baikonur space center</a> in Kazakhstan on board a <a href="/wiki/Zenit-3F" title="Zenit-3F">Zenit 3F</a> rocket. The satellite was built by Russia\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RSC_Energia" title="RSC Energia">RSC Energia</a>, a subsidiary of the state-run space industry player <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">Roscosmos</a>. The satellite payload was supplied by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_%26_Space" title="Airbus Defence &amp; Space">Airbus Defence &amp; Space</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Due to an on-board power failure during solar panel deployment, on 27 December, RSC Energia revealed that they lost communications contact with the satellite. Although, subsequent attempts to restore communications with the satellite were successful, the satellite eventually stopped sending data and RSC Energia confirmed that AngoSat-1 was inoperable. The launch of AngoSat-1 was aimed at ensuring telecommunications throughout the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> According to Aristides Safeca, Secretary of State for Telecommunications, the satellite was aimed at providing telecommunications services, TV, internet and <a href="/wiki/E-government" title="E-government">e-government</a> and was expected to remain in orbit "at best" for 18 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> A replacement satellite named AngoSat-2 is in the works and is expected to be in service by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The management of the <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a> \'.ao\' passed from <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> to Angola in 2015, following new legislation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> A joint decree of minister of Telecommunications and Information Technologies Jos&#233; Carvalho da Rocha and the minister of Science and Technology, Maria C&#226;ndida Pereira Teixeira, states that "under the massification" of that Angolan domain, "conditions are created for the transfer of the domain root \'.ao\' of Portugal to Angola".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Angola" title="Demographics of Angola">Demographics of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="727" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png/220px-Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png/330px-Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png/440px-Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Population_Pyramid_2012.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population Pyramid of Angola in 2012</div></div></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Angola<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">4.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">13.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2014</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">25.8\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Angola has a population of 24,383,301 inhabitants according to the preliminary results of its 2014 census, the first one conducted or carried out since 15 December 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INE_Angola_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-INE_Angola-1">[1]</a></sup> It is composed of <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> (language <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>) 37%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Mbundu_people" title="Northern Mbundu people">Ambundu</a> (language <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a>) 23%, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a> 13%, and 32% other ethnic groups (including the <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_people" title="Chokwe people">Chokwe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ovambo_people" title="Ovambo people">Ovambo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ganguela" title="Ganguela">Ganguela</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Xindonga" title="Xindonga">Xindonga</a>) as well as about 2% <i><a href="/wiki/Mesti%C3%A7o" title="Mesti&#231;o">mesti&#231;os</a></i> (mixed European and African), 1.6% Chinese and 1% European.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-44">[44]</a></sup> The Ambundu and Ovimbundu ethnic groups combined form a majority of the population, at 62%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The population is forecast to grow to over 60 million people to 2050, 2.7 times the 2014 population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> However, on 23 March 2016, official data revealed by Angola\'s National Statistic Institute &#8211; Instituto Nacional de Estat&#237;stica (INE), states that Angola has a population of 25.789.024 inhabitants.\n</p><p>It is estimated that Angola was host to 12,100 refugees and 2,900 asylum seekers by the end of 2007. 11,400 of those refugees were originally from the Democratic Republic of Congo, who arrived in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> As of  2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> there were an estimated 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> migrant workers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> at least 220,000 <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angolans" title="Portuguese Angolans">Portuguese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Observat&#243;rio_da_Emigra&#231;&#227;o_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Observat&#243;rio_da_Emigra&#231;&#227;o-115">[115]</a></sup> and about 259,000 <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Angola" title="Chinese people in Angola">Chinese living in Angola</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 2003, more than 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> migrants have been expelled from Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Prior to independence in 1975, Angola had a community of approximately 350,000 Portuguese,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> but the vast majority left after independence and the ensuing civil war. However, Angola has recovered its Portuguese minority in recent years; currently, there are about 200,000 registered with the consulates, and increasing due to the debt crisis in Portugal and the relative prosperity in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The Chinese population stands at 258,920, mostly composed of temporary migrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Also, there is a small <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> community of about 5,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> of Angola is 5.54 children born per woman (2012 estimates), the 11th highest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_44-3"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-44">[44]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Multiple_issues plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-multiple_issues compact-ambox" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" decoding="async" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span"><div class="mw-collapsible" style="width:95%; margin: 0.2em 0;"><b>This section has multiple issues.</b> Please help <b><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">improve it</a></b> or discuss these issues on the <b><a href="/wiki/Talk:Angola" title="Talk:Angola">talk page</a></b>. <small><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Angola" title="Languages of Angola">Languages of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg/220px-Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg/330px-Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg/440px-Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angola_Ethnic_map_1970.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethnic groups of Angola 1970</div></div></div>\n<p>The languages in Angola are those originally spoken by the different ethnic groups and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, introduced during the Portuguese colonial era. The most widely spoken indigenous languages are <a href="/wiki/Umbundu" title="Umbundu">Umbundu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kikongo" title="Kikongo">Kikongo</a>, in that order. Portuguese is the official language of the country.\n</p><p>Although the exact numbers of those fluent in Portuguese or who speak Portuguese as a first language are unknown, a 2012 study mentions that Portuguese is the first language of 39% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> In 2014, a census carried out by the Instituto Nacional de Estat&#237;stica in Angola mentions that 71.15% of the nearly 25.8 million inhabitants of Angola (meaning around 18.3 million people) use Portuguese as a first or second language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Angola:_portugu&#234;s_&#233;_falado_por_71,15%_de_angolanos_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Angola:_portugu&#234;s_&#233;_falado_por_71,15%_de_angolanos-124">[124]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Angola" title="Religion in Angola">Religion in Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Angola" title="Christianity in Angola">Christianity in Angola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola" title="Islam in Angola">Islam in Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Igreja_Benguela,_Angola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1317" data-file-width="1805" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Igreja_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/220px-Igreja_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Igreja_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/330px-Igreja_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Igreja_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg/440px-Igreja_Benguela%2C_Angola.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Igreja_Benguela,_Angola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Catholic church in Benguela</div></div></div>\n<p>There are about 1,000 religious communities, mostly Christian, in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> While reliable statistics are nonexistent, estimates have it that more than half of the population are Catholics, while about a quarter adhere to the Protestant churches introduced during the colonial period: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congregationalist" title="Congregationalist">Congregationalists</a> mainly among the <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a> of the Central Highlands and the coastal region to its west, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodists" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> concentrating on the <a href="/wiki/Kimbundu" title="Kimbundu">Kimbundu</a> speaking strip from Luanda to Malanje, the <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> almost exclusively among the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a> of the north-west (now present in Luanda as well) and dispersed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventists" title="Adventists">Adventists</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed" title="Reformed">Reformed</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> In Luanda and region there subsists a nucleus of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syncretic" title="Syncretic">syncretic</a>" <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tocoists&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tocoists (page does not exist)">Tocoists</a> and in the north-west a sprinkling of <a href="/wiki/Kimbanguism" title="Kimbanguism">Kimbanguism</a> can be found, spreading from the Congo/Za&#239;re. Since independence, hundreds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> and similar communities have sprung up in the cities, where by now about 50% of the population is living; several of these communities/churches are of Brazilian origin.\n</p><p>As of  2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_State" title="U.S. Department of State">U.S. Department of State</a> estimates the Muslim population at 80,000&#8211;90,000, less than 1% of the population,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola" title="Islam in Angola">Islamic Community of Angola</a> puts the figure closer to 500,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Muslims consist largely of migrants from West Africa and the Middle East (especially <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>), although some are local converts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-customs_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-customs-130">[130]</a></sup> The Angolan government does not <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Angola#Legal_status" title="Islam in Angola">legally recognize</a> any Muslim organizations and often shuts down mosques or prevents their construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRFR2012_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR2012-131">[131]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In a study assessing nations\' levels of religious regulation and persecution with scores ranging from 0 to 10 where 0 represented low levels of regulation or persecution, Angola was scored 0.8 on Government Regulation of Religion, 4.0 on Social Regulation of Religion, 0 on Government Favoritism of Religion and 0 on Religious Persecution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Foreign <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> were very active prior to independence in 1975, although since the beginning of the anti-colonial fight in 1961 the Portuguese colonial authorities expelled a series of Protestant missionaries and closed mission stations based on the belief that the missionaries were inciting pro-independence sentiments. Missionaries have been able to return to the country since the early 1990s, although security conditions due to the civil war have prevented them until 2002 from restoring many of their former inland mission stations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Catholic Church and some major Protestant denominations mostly keep to themselves in contrast to the "New Churches" which actively proselytize. Catholics, as well as some major Protestant denominations, provide help for the poor in the form of crop seeds, farm animals, medical care and education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table
