style="text-align:right;">67,553\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Angola" title="Health in Angola">Health in Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_(5686703351).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg/220px-Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg/330px-Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg/440px-Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_%285686703351%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angolan_woman_with_children_outside_health_clinic_(5686703351).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Angolan woman with children outside a health clinic</div></div></div>\n<p>Epidemics of <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabies" title="Rabies">rabies</a> and African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemorrhagic" title="Hemorrhagic">hemorrhagic</a> fevers like <a href="/wiki/Marburg_virus" title="Marburg virus">Marburg hemorrhagic fever</a>, are common diseases in several parts of the country. Many regions in this country have high incidence rates of <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and high <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS in Africa">HIV prevalence</a> rates. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dengue" title="Dengue">Dengue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filariasis" title="Filariasis">filariasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leishmaniasis" title="Leishmaniasis">leishmaniasis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Onchocerciasis" title="Onchocerciasis">onchocerciasis</a> (river blindness) are other diseases carried by insects that also occur in the region. Angola has one of the highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rates</a> in the world and one of the world\'s lowest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancies" title="Life expectancies">life expectancies</a>. A 2007 survey concluded that low and deficient <a href="/wiki/Niacin" title="Niacin">niacin</a> status was common in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> is currently conducting several surveys in Angola on malaria, domestic violence and more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Angola_Surveys_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-Angola_Surveys-137">[137]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2014, the Angolan Institute for Cancer Control (IACC) was created by presidential decree, and it will integrate the National Health Service in Angola.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The purpose of this new centre is to ensure health and medical care in <a href="/wiki/Oncology" title="Oncology">oncology</a>, policy implementation, programmes and plans for prevention and specialised treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> This cancer institute will be assumed as a reference institution in the central and southern regions of Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, Angola launched a national campaign of <a href="/wiki/Vaccination" title="Vaccination">vaccination</a> against <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, extended to every child under ten years old and aiming to go to all 18 provinces in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The measure is part of the Strategic Plan for the Elimination of Measles 2014&#8211;2020 created by the Angolan Ministry of Health which includes strengthening routine immunisation, a proper dealing with measles cases, national campaigns, introducing a second dose of vaccination in the national routine vaccination calendar and active epidemiological surveillance for measles. This campaign took place together with the vaccination against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_A" title="Vitamin A">vitamin A</a> supplementation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/2016_Angola_and_DR_Congo_yellow_fever_outbreak" title="2016 Angola and DR Congo yellow fever outbreak">yellow fever</a> outbreak, the worst in the country in three decades<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> began in December 2015. By August 2016, when the outbreak began to subside, nearly 4,000 people were suspected of being infected. As many as 369 may have died. The outbreak began in the capital, Luanda, and spread to at least 16 of the 18 provinces.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Angola" title="Education in Angola">Education in Angola</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda,_Angola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg/220px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg/330px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg/440px-Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda%2C_Angola.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lyceum_Salvador_Correia_in_Luanda,_Angola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lyceum Salvador Correia in Luanda</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kuito_class.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kuito_class.jpg/220px-Kuito_class.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kuito_class.jpg/330px-Kuito_class.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kuito_class.jpg/440px-Kuito_class.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kuito_class.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kuito class, Angola</div></div></div>\n<p>Although by law education in Angola is compulsory and free for eight years, the government reports that a percentage of pupils are not attending due to a lack of school buildings and teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> Pupils are often responsible for paying additional school-related expenses, including fees for books and supplies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, the gross primary enrollment rate was 74 percent and in 1998, the most recent year for which data are available, the net primary enrollment rate was 61 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-2"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> Gross and net enrollment ratios are based on the number of pupils formally registered in primary school and therefore do not necessarily reflect actual school attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-3"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> There continue to be significant disparities in enrollment between rural and urban areas. In 1995, 71.2 percent of children ages 7 to 14 years were attending school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-4"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> It is reported that higher percentages of boys attend school than girls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-5"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Angolan_Civil_War" title="Angolan Civil War">Angolan Civil War</a> (1975&#8211;2002), nearly half of all schools were reportedly looted and destroyed, leading to current problems with overcrowding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-6"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ministry of Education recruited 20,000 new teachers in 2005 and continued to implement teacher trainings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-7"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> Teachers tend to be underpaid, inadequately trained and overworked (sometimes teaching two or three shifts a day).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-8"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> Some teachers may reportedly demand payment or bribes directly from their pupils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-9"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> Other factors, such as the presence of landmines, lack of resources and identity papers, and poor health prevent children from regularly attending school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-10"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup> Although budgetary allocations for education were increased in 2004, the education system in Angola continues to be extremely under-funded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_144-11"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to estimates by the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UNESCO Institute for Statistics</a>, the adult literacy rate in 2011 was 70.4%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unescolit_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-unescolit-145">[145]</a></sup> By 2015, this had increased to 71.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> 82.9% of males and 54.2% of women are literate as of 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Since independence from Portugal in 1975, a number of Angolan students continued to be admitted every year at high schools, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Politechnic" title="Politechnic">polytechnical</a> institutes and universities in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, Brazil and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> through bilateral agreements; in general, these students belong to the elites.\n</p><p>In September 2014, the Angolan Ministry of Education announced an investment of 16 million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euros</a> in the computerisation of over 300 classrooms across the country. The project also includes training teachers at a national level, "as a way to introduce and use new information technologies in primary schools, thus reflecting an improvement in the quality of teaching."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, the Angolan government started building the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Angolan_Media_Libraries_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Angolan Media Libraries Network (page does not exist)">Angolan Media Libraries Network</a>, distributed throughout several provinces in the country to facilitate the people\'s access to information and knowledge. Each site has a bibliographic archive, multimedia resources and computers with Internet access, as well as areas for reading, researching and socialising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The plan envisages the establishment of one media library in each Angolan province by 2017. The project also includes the implementation of several media libraries, in order to provide the several contents available in the fixed media libraries to the most isolated populations in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> At this time, the mobile media libraries are already operating in the provinces of Luanda, Malanje, U&#237;ge, Cabinda and Lunda South. As for REMA, the provinces of Luanda, Benguela, Lubango and Soyo have currently working media libraries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Angola" title="Culture of Angola">Culture of Angola</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Angola" title="Music of Angola">Music of Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angolan_cuisine" title="Angolan cuisine">Angolan cuisine</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3738" data-file-width="2670" decoding="async" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/220px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/330px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg/440px-African_Art%2C_Yombe_sculpture%2C_Louvre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:African_Art,_Yombe_sculpture,_Louvre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yombe_people" title="Yombe people">Yombe</a>-sculpture, 19th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substratum" title="Substratum">substrate</a></i> of Angolan culture is African, predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_people" title="Bantu people">Bantu</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Portuguese culture</a> has had a significant impact, specifically in terms of language and religion. The diverse ethnic communities &#8211; the <a href="/wiki/Ovimbundu" title="Ovimbundu">Ovimbundu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Mbundu_people" title="Northern Mbundu people">Ambundu</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bakongo" title="Bakongo">Bakongo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chokwe_people" title="Chokwe people">Chokwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbunda_people" title="Mbunda people">Mbunda</a> and other peoples &#8211; to varying degrees maintain their own cultural traits, traditions and languages, but in the cities, where slightly more than half of the population now lives, a mixed culture has been emerging since colonial times; in <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, since its foundation in the 16th century. In this urban culture, the Portuguese heritage has become more and more dominant. African roots are evident in music and dance, and is moulding the way in which Portuguese is spoken. This process is well reflected in contemporary Angolan literature, especially in the works of <a href="/wiki/Angolan_literature" title="Angolan literature">Angolan authors</a>.\n</p><p>In 2014, Angola resumed the National Festival of Angolan Culture after a 25-year break. The festival took place in all the provincial capitals and lasted for 20 days, with the theme <i>Culture as a Factor of Peace and Development</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1972, one of Angola\'s first feature films, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Maldoror" title="Sarah Maldoror">Sarah Maldoror</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Co-production_(media)" title="Co-production (media)">internationally co-produced</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Sambizanga_(film)" title="Sambizanga (film)">Sambizanga</a></i>, was released at the <a href="/wiki/Carthage_Film_Festival" title="Carthage Film Festival">Carthage Film Festival</a> to critical acclaim, winning the <i>Tanit d\'Or</i>, the festival\'s highest prize.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg/220px-Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg/330px-Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg/440px-Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadio-11Nov-Luanda_03_linke-Seite-Bogen_LWS-2011-08-NC_0991.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of 11 November stadium in Luanda, Angola, with Tribunes and running track</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a> is the most popular sport in Angola. Its <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_basketball_team" title="Angola national basketball team">national team</a> has won the <a href="/wiki/AfroBasket" title="AfroBasket">AfroBasket</a> 11 times and holds the record of most titles. As a top team in Africa, it\'s a regular competitor at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the Summer Olympics">Summer Olympic Games</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Cup" title="FIBA World Cup">FIBA World Cup</a>.\nIn football, Angola hosted the <a href="/wiki/2010_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2010 Africa Cup of Nations">2010 Africa Cup of Nations</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Angola_national_football_team" title="Angola national football team">Angola national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, as this was their first appearance on the World Cup finals stage. They were eliminated after one defeat and two draws in the group stage. They won 3 <a href="/wiki/COSAFA_Cup" title="COSAFA Cup">COSAFA Cups</a> and finished runner up in <a href="/wiki/2011_African_Nations_Championship" title="2011 African Nations Championship">2011 African Nations Championship</a>. Angola has participated in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Women%27s_Handball_Championship" title="World Women\'s Handball Championship">World Women\'s Handball Championship</a> for several years. The country has also appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Angola_at_the_Olympics" title="Angola at the Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> for seven years and both regularly competes in and once has hosted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIRS_Roller_Hockey_World_Cup" title="FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup">FIRS Roller Hockey World Cup</a>, where the best finish is sixth. Angola is also often believed to have historic roots in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martial_art" title="Martial art">martial art</a> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capoeira_Angola" title="Capoeira Angola">Capoeira Angola</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Batuque_(game)" title="Batuque (game)">Batuque</a>" which were practiced by <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Angola" title="Slavery in Angola">enslaved African Angolans</a> transported as part of the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Africa" title="Portal:Africa">Africa portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Angola" title="Outline of Angola">Outline of Angola</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Index_of_Angola-related_articles" title="Index of Angola-related articles">Index of Angola-related articles</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Angola&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-INE_Angola-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-INE_Angola_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-INE_Angola_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" Angola)</a> <a class="external text" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 6 May 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-imf2-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a
